2b:["$","p",null,{"className":"x:not-first:mt-[1.25em] x:leading-7","children":["This isn’t surprising. ",["$","a",null,{"href":"https://arxiv.org/abs/2409.03797","target":"_blank","rel":"noreferrer","className":"x:focus-visible:nextra-focus x:text-primary-600 x:underline x:hover:no-underline x:decoration-from-font x:[text-underline-position:from-font]","children":["NESTFUL (EMNLP 2025)",[" ",["$","svg",null,{"fill":"none","stroke":"currentColor","strokeLinecap":"round","strokeLinejoin":"round","strokeWidth":1.7,"viewBox":"0 0 24 24","height":"1em","className":"x:inline x:align-baseline x:shrink-0","children":[["$","path",null,{"d":"M7 17L17 7"}],["$","path",null,{"d":"M7 7h10v10"}]]}]]]}]," measured GPT-4o at 28% accuracy on nested tool call sequences. ",["$","a",null,{"href":"https://arxiv.org/abs/2501.10868","target":"_blank","rel":"noreferrer","className":"x:focus-visible:nextra-focus x:text-primary-600 x:underline x:hover:no-underline x:decoration-from-font x:[text-underline-position:from-font]","children":["JSONSchemaBench (ICLR 2025)",[" ",["$","svg",null,{"fill":"none","stroke":"currentColor","strokeLinecap":"round","strokeLinejoin":"round","strokeWidth":1.7,"viewBox":"0 0 24 24","height":"1em","className":"x:inline x:align-baseline x:shrink-0","children":[["$","path",null,{"d":"M7 17L17 7"}],["$","path",null,{"d":"M7 7h10v10"}]]}]]]}]," tested constrained decoding frameworks on 10,000 real-world schemas and found 3–41% coverage on the hardest ones. The consensus is clear: function calling works for flat, simple schemas. For anything with recursive nesting or deep structural complexity, don’t bother."]}]
2c:["$","p",null,{"className":"x:not-first:mt-[1.25em] x:leading-7","children":"But if you want to make AI output deterministic — parse it, validate it, and correct it in a loop until it converges — there is no alternative to structured output. Free-form text can’t be mechanically verified. Natural language can’t be compiled. Without structure, there’s no feedback loop, and without a feedback loop, there’s no guarantee. So we didn’t have the luxury of giving up on function calling. We had to make it work on the exact kind of complex, recursive schemas the industry had written off."}]
2d:["$","p",null,{"className":"x:not-first:mt-[1.25em] x:leading-7","children":[["$","a",null,{"href":"https://github.com/wrtnlabs/autobe","target":"_blank","rel":"noreferrer","className":"x:focus-visible:nextra-focus x:text-primary-600 x:underline x:hover:no-underline x:decoration-from-font x:[text-underline-position:from-font]","children":["AutoBe",[" ",["$","svg",null,{"fill":"none","stroke":"currentColor","strokeLinecap":"round","strokeLinejoin":"round","strokeWidth":1.7,"viewBox":"0 0 24 24","height":"1em","className":"x:inline x:align-baseline x:shrink-0","children":[["$","path",null,{"d":"M7 17L17 7"}],["$","path",null,{"d":"M7 7h10v10"}]]}]]]}]," is the result. Hook up that 6.75% model and what happens? Final compilation success rate: ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"99.8%+"}],". All five Qwen models."]}]
2e:["$","p",null,{"className":"x:not-first:mt-[1.25em] x:leading-7","children":["The answer wasn’t a better model or a smarter prompt. It was a ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"harness"}]," — type schemas that constrain outputs, compilers that verify results, and structured feedback that pinpoints exactly where and why something went wrong so the LLM can correct itself. A deterministic loop wrapping a probabilistic model. The engineering outside the model, not inside, that made the difference."]}]

63:["$","p",null,{"className":"x:not-first:mt-[1.25em] x:leading-7","children":["This is the key point. The schema generated by the Typia compiler from source code types powers every runtime function that follows. The schema that ",["$","code",null,{"className":"nextra-code","dir":"ltr","children":"parse()"}]," references when recovering broken JSON and coercing types, the schema that ",["$","code",null,{"className":"nextra-code","dir":"ltr","children":"validate()"}]," uses as the comparison target when diagnosing errors — they’re all the same schema, automatically generated from types at compile time. 99:["$","p",null,{"className":"x:not-first:mt-[1.25em] x:leading-7","children":"“Don’t think of a pink elephant.” The first thing that comes to mind is a pink elephant. When you tell an LLM “don’t do X,” X gets placed at the center of attention. To avoid a forbidden pattern, the model must first recall that pattern, which paradoxically increases its generation probability. This is the essence of token prediction."}]
